```
1. //! Composer-side Ctrl+R reverse history search state and rendering helpers.
2. //!
3. //! The persistent and local history stores live in `chat_composer_history`, but the composer owns
4. //! the active search session because it has to snapshot/restore the editable draft, preview matches
5. //! in the textarea, and render the footer prompt while the footer line is acting as the search
6. //! input.
7. //!
8. //! This module is responsible for the UI-facing lifecycle of a search session: recognizing the
9. //! keys that enter and drive search mode, keeping the footer query separate from the textarea
10. //! preview, restoring the original draft on cancellation or misses, and translating history search
11. //! results into composer-visible state. It deliberately does not decide which history entries
12. //! match, how duplicate results are skipped, or when persistent history should be fetched; those
13. //! traversal invariants stay with `ChatComposerHistory`.
14. //!
15. //! A search session starts idle with an empty footer query, so opening Ctrl+R never previews the
16. //! latest history entry by itself. Typing a query restarts traversal from newest to oldest,
17. //! repeated Ctrl+R/Up and Ctrl+S/Down move between unique matches, `Enter` accepts the current
18. //! preview as an editable draft, and `Esc` or Ctrl+C restores the exact draft that existed before
19. //! search started.
20. 
21. use std::ops::Range;
22. 
23. use crossterm::event::KeyCode;
24. use crossterm::event::KeyEvent;
25. use crossterm::event::KeyEventKind;
26. use crossterm::event::KeyModifiers;
27. use ratatui::layout::Constraint;
28. use ratatui::layout::Layout;
29. use ratatui::layout::Rect;
30. use ratatui::style::Stylize;
31. use ratatui::text::Line;
32. use ratatui::text::Span;
33. 
34. use super::super::chat_composer_history::HistorySearchDirection;
35. use super::super::chat_composer_history::HistorySearchResult;
36. use super::super::footer::footer_height;
37. use super::super::footer::reset_mode_after_activity;
38. use super::ActivePopup;
39. use super::ChatComposer;
40. use super::ComposerDraft;
41. use super::InputResult;
42. use crate::app_event::AppEvent;
43. use crate::key_hint;
44. use crate::key_hint::KeyBinding;
45. use crate::key_hint::KeyBindingListExt;
46. use crate::key_hint::has_ctrl_or_alt;
47. use crate::ui_consts::FOOTER_INDENT_COLS;
48. 
49. /// Active composer-owned state for one Ctrl+R search interaction.
50. ///
51. /// The session is created only by [`ChatComposer::begin_history_search`] and is cleared only by
52. /// accepting, canceling, or replacing the search mode. It stores the original draft separately from
53. /// the footer query so transient previews never destroy the user's in-progress composer content.
54. #[derive(Clone, Debug)]
55. pub(super) struct HistorySearchSession {
56.     /// Draft to restore when search is canceled or a query has no match.
57.     original_draft: ComposerDraft,
58.     /// Footer-owned query text typed while Ctrl+R search is active.
59.     query: String,
60.     /// User-visible search status used to choose footer hints and composer preview behavior.
61.     status: HistorySearchStatus,
62. }
63. 
64. /// User-visible phase of the active Ctrl+R search session.
65. ///
66. /// Search keeps the footer query and the composer preview separate: `Idle` leaves the original
67. /// draft untouched, `Searching` waits for persistent history, `Match` previews a found entry, and
68. /// `NoMatch` restores the original draft while leaving the search input open for more typing.
69. #[derive(Clone, Debug)]
70. enum HistorySearchStatus {
71.     Idle,
72.     Searching,
73.     Match,
74.     NoMatch,
75. }
76. 
77. impl ChatComposer {
78.     #[cfg(test)]
79.     pub(super) fn history_search_active(&self) -> bool {
80.         self.history_search.is_some()
81.     }
82. 
83.     /// Returns whether a key event should open reverse history search or step to an older match.
84.     ///
85.     /// The check accepts both normal Ctrl+R reports and the raw control character variant that
86.     /// some terminals emit. Callers should only use this before generic text handling; treating the
87.     /// raw control character as ordinary input would insert an invisible byte into the search query
88.     /// or composer draft.
89.     pub(super) fn is_history_search_key(key_event: &KeyEvent, bindings: &[KeyBinding]) -> bool {
90.         bindings.is_pressed(*key_event)
91.     }
92. 
93.     fn is_history_search_forward_key(key_event: &KeyEvent, bindings: &[KeyBinding]) -> bool {
94.         bindings.is_pressed(*key_event)
95.     }
96. 
97.     /// Opens footer-owned reverse history search without previewing history yet.
98.     ///
99.     /// Entering search mode first flushes pending paste-burst text, then snapshots the full
100.     /// composer draft, clears any file/search popup state, and resets history traversal. The first
101.     /// visible match is produced only after the footer query becomes non-empty, which keeps Ctrl+R
102.     /// from replacing an empty composer with the latest prompt before the user has searched for
103.     /// anything.
104.     pub(super) fn begin_history_search(&mut self) -> (InputResult, bool) {
105.         if let Some(pasted) = self.draft.paste_burst.flush_before_modified_input() {
106.             self.handle_paste(pasted);
107.         }
108.         self.draft.paste_burst.clear_window_after_non_char();
109. 
110.         if self.popups.current_file_query.is_some() {
111.             self.app_event_tx
112.                 .send(AppEvent::StartFileSearch(String::new()));
113.             self.popups.current_file_query = None;
114.         }
115.         self.popups.active = ActivePopup::None;
116.         self.attachments.clear_remote_image_selection();
117.         self.history_search = Some(HistorySearchSession {
118.             original_draft: self.snapshot_draft(),
119.             query: String::new(),
120.             status: HistorySearchStatus::Idle,
121.         });
122.         self.history.reset_search();
123.         (InputResult::None, true)
124.     }
125. 
126.     /// Handles every key while the footer is acting as the history search input.
127.     ///
128.     /// The method consumes search-mode keys before normal composer editing sees them. It guarantees
129.     /// that `Esc` and Ctrl+C restore the original draft, `Enter` only accepts an actual match, plain
130.     /// characters edit the footer query, and navigation keys delegate traversal to
131.     /// `ChatComposerHistory`. Calling this when no search session exists is harmless for ignored
132.     /// keys but would make query-edit branches no-op, so route here only after
133.     /// `history_search.is_some()` has been established.
134.     pub(super) fn handle_history_search_key(&mut self, key_event: KeyEvent) -> (InputResult, bool) {
135.         if key_event.kind == KeyEventKind::Release {
136.             return (InputResult::None, false);
137.         }
138. 
139.         if Self::is_history_search_key(&key_event, &self.history_search_previous_keys)
140.             || matches!(key_event.code, KeyCode::Up)
141.         {
142.             let result = self.history_search_in_direction(HistorySearchDirection::Older);
143.             return (result, true);
144.         }
145. 
146.         if Self::is_history_search_forward_key(&key_event, &self.history_search_next_keys)
147.             || matches!(key_event.code, KeyCode::Down)
148.         {
149.             let result = self.history_search_in_direction(HistorySearchDirection::Newer);
150.             return (result, true);
151.         }
152. 
153.         match key_event {
154.             KeyEvent {
155.                 code: KeyCode::Esc, ..
156.             } => {
157.                 self.cancel_history_search();
158.                 (InputResult::None, true)
159.             }
160.             KeyEvent {
161.                 code: KeyCode::Char(c),
162.                 modifiers,
163.                 ..
164.             } if modifiers.contains(KeyModifiers::CONTROL) && c.eq_ignore_ascii_case(&'c') => {
165.                 self.cancel_history_search();
166.                 (InputResult::None, true)
167.             }
168.             KeyEvent {
169.                 code: KeyCode::Char('\u{0003}'),
170.                 modifiers: KeyModifiers::NONE,
171.                 ..
172.             } => {
173.                 self.cancel_history_search();
174.                 (InputResult::None, true)
175.             }
176.             KeyEvent {
177.                 code: KeyCode::Enter,
178.                 modifiers: KeyModifiers::NONE,
179.                 ..
180.             } => {
181.                 if self
182.                     .history_search
183.                     .as_ref()
184.                     .is_some_and(|search| matches!(search.status, HistorySearchStatus::Match))
185.                 {
186.                     self.history_search = None;
187.                     self.history.reset_search();
188.                     self.footer.mode = reset_mode_after_activity(self.footer.mode);
189.                     self.move_cursor_to_end();
190.                 }
191.                 (InputResult::None, true)
192.             }
193.             KeyEvent {
194.                 code: KeyCode::Backspace,
195.                 ..
196.             }
197.             | KeyEvent {
198.                 code: KeyCode::Char('h'),
199.                 modifiers: KeyModifiers::CONTROL,
200.                 ..
201.             } => {
202.                 if let Some(search) = self.history_search.as_ref() {
203.                     let mut query = search.query.clone();
204.                     query.pop();
205.                     self.update_history_search_query(query);
206.                 }
207.                 (InputResult::None, true)
208.             }
209.             KeyEvent {
210.                 code: KeyCode::Char('u'),
211.                 modifiers: KeyModifiers::CONTROL,
212.                 ..
213.             } => {
214.                 self.update_history_search_query(String::new());
215.                 (InputResult::None, true)
216.             }
217.             KeyEvent {
218.                 code: KeyCode::Char(ch),
219.                 modifiers,
220.                 ..
221.             } if !has_ctrl_or_alt(modifiers) => {
222.                 if let Some(search) = self.history_search.as_ref() {
223.                     let mut query = search.query.clone();
224.                     query.push(ch);
225.                     self.update_history_search_query(query);
226.                 }
227.                 (InputResult::None, true)
228.             }
229.             _ => (InputResult::None, true),
230.         }
231.     }
232. 
233.     fn history_search_in_direction(&mut self, direction: HistorySearchDirection) -> InputResult {
234.         let Some((query, original_draft)) = self
235.             .history_search
236.             .as_ref()
237.             .map(|search| (search.query.clone(), search.original_draft.clone()))
238.         else {
239.             return InputResult::None;
240.         };
```

</details>

1. use std::path::PathBuf;
2. 
3. use codex_file_search::FileMatch;
4. use ratatui::buffer::Buffer;
5. use ratatui::layout::Rect;
6. use ratatui::widgets::WidgetRef;
7. 
8. use crate::render::Insets;
9. use crate::render::RectExt;
10. 
11. use super::popup_consts::MAX_POPUP_ROWS;
12. use super::scroll_state::ScrollState;
13. use super::selection_popup_common::GenericDisplayRow;
14. use super::selection_popup_common::render_rows;
15. 
16. /// Visual state for the file-search popup.
17. pub(crate) struct FileSearchPopup {
18.     /// Query corresponding to the `matches` currently shown.
19.     display_query: String,
20.     /// Latest query typed by the user. May differ from `display_query` when
21.     /// a search is still in-flight.
22.     pending_query: String,
23.     /// When `true` we are still waiting for results for `pending_query`.
24.     waiting: bool,
25.     /// Cached matches; paths relative to the search dir.
26.     matches: Vec<FileMatch>,
27.     /// Shared selection/scroll state.
28.     state: ScrollState,
29. }
30. 
31. impl FileSearchPopup {
32.     pub(crate) fn new() -> Self {
33.         Self {
34.             display_query: String::new(),
35.             pending_query: String::new(),
36.             waiting: true,
37.             matches: Vec::new(),
38.             state: ScrollState::new(),
39.         }
40.     }
41. 
42.     /// Update the query and reset state to *waiting*.
43.     pub(crate) fn set_query(&mut self, query: &str) {
44.         if query == self.pending_query {
45.             return;
46.         }
47. 
48.         self.pending_query.clear();
49.         self.pending_query.push_str(query);
50. 
51.         self.waiting = true; // waiting for new results
52.     }
53. 
54.     /// Put the popup into an "idle" state used for an empty query (just "@").
55.     /// Shows a hint instead of matches until the user types more characters.
56.     pub(crate) fn set_empty_prompt(&mut self) {
57.         self.display_query.clear();
58.         self.pending_query.clear();
59.         self.waiting = false;
60.         self.matches.clear();
61.         // Reset selection/scroll state when showing the empty prompt.
62.         self.state.reset();
63.     }
64. 
65.     /// Replace matches when a `FileSearchResult` arrives.
66.     /// Replace matches. Only applied when `query` matches `pending_query`.
67.     pub(crate) fn set_matches(&mut self, query: &str, matches: Vec<FileMatch>) {
68.         if query != self.pending_query {
69.             return; // stale
70.         }
71. 
72.         self.display_query = query.to_string();
73.         self.matches = matches.into_iter().take(MAX_POPUP_ROWS).collect();
74.         self.waiting = false;
75.         let len = self.matches.len();
76.         self.state.clamp_selection(len);
77.         self.state.ensure_visible(len, len.min(MAX_POPUP_ROWS));
78.     }
79. 
80.     /// Move selection cursor up.
81.     pub(crate) fn move_up(&mut self) {
82.         let len = self.matches.len();
83.         self.state.move_up_wrap(len);
84.         self.state.ensure_visible(len, len.min(MAX_POPUP_ROWS));
85.     }
86. 
87.     /// Move selection cursor down.
88.     pub(crate) fn move_down(&mut self) {
89.         let len = self.matches.len();
90.         self.state.move_down_wrap(len);
91.         self.state.ensure_visible(len, len.min(MAX_POPUP_ROWS));
92.     }
93. 
94.     pub(crate) fn selected_match(&self) -> Option<&PathBuf> {
95.         self.state
96.             .selected_idx
97.             .and_then(|idx| self.matches.get(idx))
98.             .map(|file_match| &file_match.path)
99.     }
100. 
101.     pub(crate) fn calculate_required_height(&self) -> u16 {
102.         // Row count depends on whether we already have matches. If no matches
103.         // yet (e.g. initial search or query with no results) reserve a single
104.         // row so the popup is still visible. When matches are present we show
105.         // up to MAX_RESULTS regardless of the waiting flag so the list
106.         // remains stable while a newer search is in-flight.
107. 
108.         self.matches.len().clamp(1, MAX_POPUP_ROWS) as u16
109.     }
110. }
111. 
112. impl WidgetRef for &FileSearchPopup {
113.     fn render_ref(&self, area: Rect, buf: &mut Buffer) {
114.         // Convert matches to GenericDisplayRow, translating indices to usize at the UI boundary.
115.         let rows_all: Vec<GenericDisplayRow> = if self.matches.is_empty() {
116.             Vec::new()
117.         } else {
118.             self.matches
119.                 .iter()
120.                 .map(|m| GenericDisplayRow {
121.                     name: m.path.to_string_lossy().to_string(),
122.                     name_prefix_spans: Vec::new(),
123.                     match_indices: m
124.                         .indices
125.                         .as_ref()
126.                         .map(|v| v.iter().map(|&i| i as usize).collect()),
127.                     display_shortcut: None,
128.                     description: None,
129.                     category_tag: None,
130.                     wrap_indent: None,
131.                     is_disabled: false,
132.                     disabled_reason: None,
133.                 })
134.                 .collect()
135.         };
136. 
137.         let empty_message = if self.waiting {
138.             "loading..."
139.         } else {
140.             "no matches"
141.         };
142. 
143.         render_rows(
144.             area.inset(Insets::tlbr(
145.                 /*top*/ 0, /*left*/ 2, /*bottom*/ 0, /*right*/ 0,
146.             )),
147.             buf,
148.             &rows_all,
149.             &self.state,
150.             MAX_POPUP_ROWS,
151.             empty_message,
152.         );
153.     }
154. }
155. 
156. #[cfg(test)]
157. mod tests {
158.     use super::*;
159.     use codex_file_search::MatchType;
160.     use pretty_assertions::assert_eq;
161. 
162.     fn file_match(index: usize) -> FileMatch {
163.         FileMatch {
164.             score: index as u32,
165.             path: PathBuf::from(format!("src/file_{index:02}.rs")),
166.             match_type: MatchType::File,
167.             root: PathBuf::from("/tmp/repo"),
168.             indices: None,
169.         }
170.     }
171. 
172.     #[test]
173.     fn set_matches_keeps_only_the_first_page_of_results() {
174.         let mut popup = FileSearchPopup::new();
175.         popup.set_query("file");
176.         popup.set_matches("file", (0..(MAX_POPUP_ROWS + 2)).map(file_match).collect());
177. 
178.         assert_eq!(
179.             popup.matches,
180.             (0..MAX_POPUP_ROWS).map(file_match).collect::<Vec<_>>()
181.         );
182.         assert_eq!(popup.calculate_required_height(), MAX_POPUP_ROWS as u16);
183.     }

1. //! Approval modal rendering and decision routing for high-risk operations.
2. //!
3. //! This module converts agent approval requests (exec/apply-patch/MCP
4. //! elicitation) into a list-selection view with action-specific options and
5. //! shortcuts. It owns two important contracts:
6. //!
7. //! 1. Selection always emits an explicit decision event back to the app.
8. //! 2. MCP elicitation keeps `Esc` mapped to `Cancel`, even with custom
9. //!    keybindings, so dismissal never silently becomes "continue without info".
10. //!
11. //! This module does not evaluate whether an action is safe to run; it only
12. //! presents choices and routes user decisions.
13.

15. use std::path::PathBuf;

70. /// Request coming from the agent that needs user approval.
71. #[derive(Clone, Debug)]
72. pub(crate) enum ApprovalRequest {
73.     Exec {
74.         thread_id: ThreadId,
75.         thread_label: Option<String>,
76.         id: String,
77.         command: Vec<String>,
78.         reason: Option<String>,
79.         available_decisions: Vec<CommandExecutionApprovalDecision>,
80.         network_approval_context: Option<NetworkApprovalContext>,
81.         additional_permissions: Option<AdditionalPermissionProfile>,
82.     },
83.     Permissions {
84.         thread_id: ThreadId,
85.         thread_label: Option<String>,
86.         call_id: String,
87.         environment_id: Option<String>,
88.         reason: Option<String>,
89.         permissions: RequestPermissionProfile,
90.     },
91.     ApplyPatch {
92.         thread_id: ThreadId,
93.         thread_label: Option<String>,
94.         id: String,
95.         reason: Option<String>,
96.         cwd: AbsolutePathBuf,
97.         changes: HashMap<PathBuf, FileChange>,
98.     },
99.     McpElicitation {
100.         thread_id: ThreadId,
101.         thread_label: Option<String>,
102.         server_name: String,
103.         request_id: RequestId,
104.         message: String,

107. 
108. impl ApprovalRequest {
109.     fn thread_id(&self) -> ThreadId {
110.         match self {
111.             ApprovalRequest::Exec { thread_id, .. }
112.             | ApprovalRequest::Permissions { thread_id, .. }
113.             | ApprovalRequest::ApplyPatch { thread_id, .. }
114.             | ApprovalRequest::McpElicitation { thread_id, .. } => *thread_id,
115.         }
116.     }
117. 
118.     fn thread_label(&self) -> Option<&str> {
119.         match self {
120.             ApprovalRequest::Exec { thread_label, .. }
121.             | ApprovalRequest::Permissions { thread_label, .. }
122.             | ApprovalRequest::ApplyPatch { thread_label, .. }
123.             | ApprovalRequest::McpElicitation { thread_label, .. } => thread_label.as_deref(),
124.         }
125.     }
126. 
127.     pub(super) fn matches_resolved_request(&self, request: &ResolvedAppServerRequest) -> bool {
128.         match (self, request) {
129.             (
130.                 ApprovalRequest::Exec { id, .. },
131.                 ResolvedAppServerRequest::ExecApproval { id: resolved_id },
132.             ) => id == resolved_id,
133.             (
134.                 ApprovalRequest::Permissions { call_id, .. },
135.                 ResolvedAppServerRequest::PermissionsApproval { id },
136.             ) => call_id == id,
137.             (
138.                 ApprovalRequest::ApplyPatch { id, .. },
139.                 ResolvedAppServerRequest::FileChangeApproval { id: resolved_id },
140.             ) => id == resolved_id,
141.             (
142.                 ApprovalRequest::McpElicitation {
143.                     server_name,
144.                     request_id,
145.                     ..
146.                 },
147.                 ResolvedAppServerRequest::McpElicitation {
148.                     server_name: resolved_server_name,
149.                     request_id: resolved_request_id,
150.                 },
151.             ) => server_name == resolved_server_name && request_id == resolved_request_id,
152.             _ => false,
153.         }
154.     }
155. }
156. 
157. /// Modal overlay asking the user to approve or deny one or more requests.
158. pub(crate) struct ApprovalOverlay {
159.     current_request: Option<ApprovalRequest>,
160.     queue: Vec<ApprovalRequest>,
161.     app_event_tx: AppEventSender,
162.     list: ListSelectionView,
163.     options: Vec<ApprovalOption>,
164.     current_complete: bool,
165.     done: bool,
166.     features: Features,
167.     approval_keymap: ApprovalKeymap,
168.     list_keymap: ListKeymap,
169. }
170. 
171. impl ApprovalOverlay {
172.     pub fn new(
173.         request: ApprovalRequest,
174.         app_event_tx: AppEventSender,
175.         features: Features,
176.         approval_keymap: ApprovalKeymap,
177.         list_keymap: ListKeymap,
178.     ) -> Self {
179.         let mut view = Self {
180.             current_request: None,
181.             queue: Vec::new(),
182.             app_event_tx: app_event_tx.clone(),
183.             list: ListSelectionView::new(Default::default(), app_event_tx, list_keymap.clone()),
184.             options: Vec::new(),
185.             current_complete: false,
186.             done: false,
187.             features,
188.             approval_keymap,
189.             list_keymap,
190.         };
191.         view.set_current(request);
192.         view
193.     }
194. 
195.     pub fn enqueue_request(&mut self, req: ApprovalRequest) {
196.         self.queue.push(req);
197.     }
198. 
199.     fn dismiss_resolved_request(&mut self, request: &ResolvedAppServerRequest) -> bool {
200.         let queue_len = self.queue.len();
201.         self.queue
202.             .retain(|queued_request| !queued_request.matches_resolved_request(request));
203.         if self
204.             .current_request
205.             .as_ref()
206.             .is_some_and(|current_request| current_request.matches_resolved_request(request))
207.         {
208.             self.current_complete = true;
209.             self.advance_queue();
210.             return true;
211.         }
212. 
213.         self.queue.len() != queue_len
214.     }
215. 
216.     fn set_current(&mut self, request: ApprovalRequest) {
217.         self.current_complete = false;
218.         let header = build_header(&request);
219.         let (options, params) = Self::build_options(
220.             &request,
221.             header,
222.             &self.features,
223.             &self.approval_keymap,
224.             &self.list_keymap,
225.         );
226.         self.current_request = Some(request);
227.         self.options = options;
228.         self.list =
229.             ListSelectionView::new(params, self.app_event_tx.clone(), self.list_keymap.clone());
230.     }
231. 
232.     fn build_options(
233.         request: &ApprovalRequest,
234.         header: Box<dyn Renderable>,
235.         _features: &Features,
236.         approval_keymap: &ApprovalKeymap,
237.         list_keymap: &ListKeymap,
238.     ) -> (Vec<ApprovalOption>, SelectionViewParams) {
239.         let (options, title) = match request {
240.             ApprovalRequest::Exec {
241.                 available_decisions,
242.                 network_approval_context,
243.                 additional_permissions,
244.                 ..
245.             } => (
246.                 exec_options(
247.                     available_decisions,
248.                     network_approval_context.as_ref(),
249.                     additional_permissions.as_ref(),
250.                     approval_keymap,
251.                 ),
252.                 network_approval_context.as_ref().map_or_else(
253.                     || "Would you like to run the following command?".to_string(),
254.                     |network_approval_context| {
255.                         format!(
256.                             "Do you want to approve network access to \"{}\"?",
257.                             network_approval_context.host
258.                         )
259.                     },
260.                 ),

1. //! Slash-command input parsing, cursor detection, and completion helpers.
2. 
3. use std::ops::Range;
4. 
5. use crossterm::event::KeyCode;
6. use crossterm::event::KeyEvent;

30. pub(super) enum SlashValidation {
31.     Immediate,
32.     Deferred,
33. }
34. 
35. pub(super) enum SubmissionValidation {
36.     Valid,
37.     UnknownCommand(String),
38. }
39. 
40. pub(super) struct InlineCommand<'a> {
41.     pub(super) command: SlashCommandItem,
42.     pub(super) rest: &'a str,
43.     pub(super) rest_offset: usize,
44. }
45. 
46. pub(super) struct SlashInput<'a> {
47.     enabled: bool,
48.     is_bash_mode: bool,
49.     command_flags: BuiltinCommandFlags,
50.     service_tier_commands: &'a [ServiceTierCommand],
51. }
52. 
53. impl<'a> SlashInput<'a> {
54.     pub(super) fn new(
55.         enabled: bool,
56.         is_bash_mode: bool,
57.         command_flags: BuiltinCommandFlags,
58.         service_tier_commands: &'a [ServiceTierCommand],
59.     ) -> Self {
60.         Self {
61.             enabled,
62.             is_bash_mode,
63.             command_flags,
64.             service_tier_commands,
65.         }
66.     }
67. 
68.     pub(super) fn validate_submission(
69.         &self,
70.         text: &str,
71.         input_starts_with_space: bool,
72.     ) -> SubmissionValidation {
73.         if !self.enabled {
74.             return SubmissionValidation::Valid;
75.         }
76.         let Some((name, _rest, _rest_offset)) = parse_slash_name(text) else {
77.             return SubmissionValidation::Valid;
78.         };
79.         if input_starts_with_space || name.contains('/') {
80.             return SubmissionValidation::Valid;
81.         }
82.         if self.command(name).is_some() {
83.             SubmissionValidation::Valid
84.         } else {
85.             SubmissionValidation::UnknownCommand(name.to_string())
86.         }
87.     }
88. 
89.     pub(super) fn bare_command(&self, text: &str) -> Option<SlashCommandItem> {
90.         if !self.enabled || self.is_bash_mode {
91.             return None;
92.         }
93.         let first_line = text.lines().next().unwrap_or("");
94.         let (name, rest, _rest_offset) = parse_slash_name(first_line)?;
95.         if !rest.is_empty() {
96.             return None;
97.         }
98.         let command = self.command(name)?;
99.         if command.supports_inline_args()
100.             && parse_slash_name(text).is_some_and(|(_, full_rest, _)| !full_rest.is_empty())
101.         {
102.             return None;
103.         }
104.         Some(command)
105.     }
106. 
107.     pub(super) fn inline_command<'text>(&self, text: &'text str) -> Option<InlineCommand<'text>> {
108.         if !self.enabled || self.is_bash_mode || text.starts_with(' ') {
109.             return None;
110.         }
111. 
112.         let (name, rest, rest_offset) = parse_slash_name(text)?;
113.         if rest.is_empty() || name.contains('/') {
114.             return None;
115.         }
116. 
117.         let command = self.command(name)?;
118.         command.supports_inline_args().then_some(InlineCommand {
119.             command,
120.             rest,
121.             rest_offset,
122.         })
123.     }
124. 
125.     pub(super) fn should_parse_on_dequeue(&self, text: &str) -> bool {
126.         self.enabled && !text.starts_with(' ') && text.trim().starts_with('/')
127.     }
128. 
129.     pub(super) fn command_element_range(
130.         &self,
131.         first_line: &str,
132.         cursor: usize,
133.     ) -> Option<Range<usize>> {
134.         if self.is_bash_mode {
135.             return None;
136.         }
137.         let (name, _rest, _rest_offset) = parse_slash_name(first_line)?;
138.         if name.contains('/') {
139.             return None;
140.         }
141.         let element_end = 1 + name.len();
142.         // A draft tail can make an in-progress prefix look complete ("/re" + "view").
143.         // Keep it editable until the cursor leaves the command name.
144.         if cursor <= first_line.len() && (1..element_end).contains(&cursor) {
145.             return None;
146.         }
147.         let has_space_after = first_line
148.             .get(element_end..)
149.             .and_then(|tail| tail.chars().next())
150.             .is_some_and(char::is_whitespace);
151.         if !has_space_after {
152.             return None;
153.         }
154.         self.command(name).is_some().then_some(0..element_end)
155.     }
156. 
157.     pub(super) fn is_editing_command_name(&self, first_line: &str, cursor: usize) -> bool {
158.         let Some((name, rest)) = command_under_cursor(first_line, cursor) else {
159.             return false;
160.         };
161.         if !self.enabled {
162.             return false;
163.         }
164.         if name.is_empty() {
165.             return rest.is_empty();
166.         }
167. 
168.         has_slash_command_prefix(name, self.command_flags, self.service_tier_commands)
169.     }
170. 
171.     pub(super) fn command_popup(&self, filter_text: &str) -> CommandPopup {
172.         let mut command_popup = CommandPopup::new(
173.             CommandPopupFlags {
174.                 collaboration_modes_enabled: self.command_flags.collaboration_modes_enabled,
175.                 connectors_enabled: self.command_flags.connectors_enabled,
176.                 plugins_command_enabled: self.command_flags.plugins_command_enabled,
177.                 service_tier_commands_enabled: self.command_flags.service_tier_commands_enabled,
178.                 goal_command_enabled: self.command_flags.goal_command_enabled,
179.                 personality_command_enabled: self.command_flags.personality_command_enabled,
180.                 realtime_conversation_enabled: self.command_flags.realtime_conversation_enabled,
181.                 audio_device_selection_enabled: self.command_flags.audio_device_selection_enabled,
182.                 windows_degraded_sandbox_active: self.command_flags.allow_elevate_sandbox,
183.                 side_conversation_active: self.command_flags.side_conversation_active,
184.             },
185.             self.service_tier_commands.to_vec(),
186.         );
187.         command_popup.on_composer_text_change(filter_text.to_string());
188.         command_popup
189.     }
190. 
191.     fn command(&self, name: &str) -> Option<SlashCommandItem> {
192.         find_slash_command(name, self.command_flags, self.service_tier_commands)
193.     }
194. }
195. 
196. pub(super) fn queued_input_action(
197.     prepared_text: &str,
198.     defer_slash_validation: bool,
199. ) -> QueuedInputAction {
200.     if defer_slash_validation && prepared_text.starts_with('/') {
201.         QueuedInputAction::ParseSlash
202.     } else if prepared_text.starts_with('!') {
203.         QueuedInputAction::RunShell
204.     } else {
205.         QueuedInputAction::Plain
206.     }
207. }
208. 
209. impl ChatComposer {
210.     /// Handle key event when the slash-command popup is visible.
211.     pub(super) fn handle_key_event_with_slash_popup(
212.         &mut self,
213.         key_event: KeyEvent,
214.     ) -> (InputResult, bool) {
215.         if self.handle_shortcut_overlay_key(&key_event) {
216.             return (InputResult::None, true);
217.         }
218.         if key_event.code == KeyCode::Esc {
219.             let next_mode = esc_hint_mode(self.footer.mode, self.is_task_running);
220.             if next_mode != self.footer.mode {
221.                 self.footer.mode = next_mode;
222.                 return (InputResult::None, true);
223.             }
224.         } else {
225.             self.footer.mode = reset_mode_after_activity(self.footer.mode);
226.         }
227.         let ActivePopup::Command(popup) = &mut self.popups.active else {
228.             unreachable!();
229.         };
230. 
231.         match key_event {
232.             KeyEvent {
233.                 code: KeyCode::Up, ..
234.             }
235.             | KeyEvent {
236.                 code: KeyCode::Char('p'),
237.                 modifiers: KeyModifiers::CONTROL,
238.                 ..
239.             } => {
240.                 popup.move_up();
```

1. use ratatui::buffer::Buffer;
2. use ratatui::layout::Rect;
3. use ratatui::widgets::WidgetRef;
4. 
5. use super::popup_consts::MAX_POPUP_ROWS;
6. use super::scroll_state::ScrollState;
7. use super::selection_popup_common::ColumnWidthConfig;
8. use super::selection_popup_common::ColumnWidthMode;
9. use super::selection_popup_common::GenericDisplayRow;
10. use super::selection_popup_common::measure_rows_height_with_col_width_mode;
11. use super::selection_popup_common::render_rows_with_col_width_mode;
12. use super::slash_commands::BuiltinCommandFlags;
13. use super::slash_commands::ServiceTierCommand;
14. use super::slash_commands::SlashCommandItem;
15. use super::slash_commands::commands_for_input;
16. use crate::render::Insets;
17. use crate::render::RectExt;
18. use crate::slash_command::SlashCommand;
19. 
20. // Hide alias commands in the default popup list so each unique action appears once.
21. // `quit` is an alias of `exit`, and `btw` is an alias of `side`, so we skip
22. // those aliases here.
23. const ALIAS_COMMANDS: &[SlashCommand] = &[SlashCommand::Quit, SlashCommand::Btw];
24. const COMMAND_COLUMN_WIDTH: ColumnWidthConfig = ColumnWidthConfig::new(
25.     ColumnWidthMode::AutoAllRows,
26.     /*name_column_width*/ None,
27. );
28. 
29. /// A selectable item in the popup.
30. #[derive(Clone, Debug, PartialEq, Eq)]
31. pub(crate) enum CommandItem {
32.     Builtin(SlashCommand),
33.     ServiceTier(ServiceTierCommand),
34. }
35. 
36. pub(crate) struct CommandPopup {
37.     command_filter: String,
38.     commands: Vec<CommandItem>,
39.     state: ScrollState,
40. }
41. 
42. #[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug, Default)]
43. pub(crate) struct CommandPopupFlags {
44.     pub(crate) collaboration_modes_enabled: bool,
45.     pub(crate) connectors_enabled: bool,
46.     pub(crate) plugins_command_enabled: bool,
47.     pub(crate) service_tier_commands_enabled: bool,
48.     pub(crate) goal_command_enabled: bool,
49.     pub(crate) personality_command_enabled: bool,
50.     pub(crate) realtime_conversation_enabled: bool,
51.     pub(crate) audio_device_selection_enabled: bool,
52.     pub(crate) windows_degraded_sandbox_active: bool,
53.     pub(crate) side_conversation_active: bool,
54. }
55. 
56. impl From<CommandPopupFlags> for BuiltinCommandFlags {
57.     fn from(value: CommandPopupFlags) -> Self {
58.         Self {
59.             collaboration_modes_enabled: value.collaboration_modes_enabled,
60.             connectors_enabled: value.connectors_enabled,
61.             plugins_command_enabled: value.plugins_command_enabled,
62.             service_tier_commands_enabled: value.service_tier_commands_enabled,
63.             goal_command_enabled: value.goal_command_enabled,
64.             personality_command_enabled: value.personality_command_enabled,
65.             realtime_conversation_enabled: value.realtime_conversation_enabled,
66.             audio_device_selection_enabled: value.audio_device_selection_enabled,
67.             allow_elevate_sandbox: value.windows_degraded_sandbox_active,
68.             side_conversation_active: value.side_conversation_active,
69.         }
70.     }
71. }
72. 
73. impl CommandPopup {
74.     pub(crate) fn new(
75.         flags: CommandPopupFlags,
76.         service_tier_commands: Vec<ServiceTierCommand>,
77.     ) -> Self {
78.         // Keep built-in availability in sync with the composer.
79.         let commands = commands_for_input(flags.into(), &service_tier_commands)
80.             .into_iter()
81.             .filter_map(|command| match command {
82.                 SlashCommandItem::Builtin(cmd) => (!cmd.command().starts_with("debug")
83.                     && cmd != SlashCommand::Apps)
84.                     .then_some(CommandItem::Builtin(cmd)),
85.                 SlashCommandItem::ServiceTier(command) => Some(CommandItem::ServiceTier(command)),
86.             })
87.             .collect();
88.         Self {
89.             command_filter: String::new(),
90.             commands,
91.             state: ScrollState::new(),
92.         }
93.     }
94. 
95.     /// Update the filter string based on the current composer text. The text
96.     /// passed in is expected to start with a leading '/'. Everything after the
97.     /// *first* '/' on the *first* line becomes the active filter that is used
98.     /// to narrow down the list of available commands.
99.     pub(crate) fn on_composer_text_change(&mut self, text: String) {
100.         let first_line = text.lines().next().unwrap_or("");
101.         let previous_filter = self.command_filter.clone();
102. 
103.         if let Some(stripped) = first_line.strip_prefix('/') {
104.             // Extract the *first* token (sequence of non-whitespace
105.             // characters) after the slash so that `/clear something` still
106.             // shows the help for `/clear`.
107.             let token = stripped.trim_start();
108.             let cmd_token = token.split_whitespace().next().unwrap_or("");
109. 
110.             // Update the filter keeping the original case (commands are all
111.             // lower-case for now but this may change in the future).
112.             self.command_filter = cmd_token.to_string();
113.         } else {
114.             // The composer no longer starts with '/'. Reset the filter so the
115.             // popup shows the *full* command list if it is still displayed
116.             // for some reason.
117.             self.command_filter.clear();
118.         }
119. 
120.         if self.command_filter != previous_filter {
121.             self.state.reset();
122.         }
123. 
124.         // Reset or clamp selected index based on new filtered list.
125.         let matches_len = self.filtered_items().len();
126.         self.state.clamp_selection(matches_len);
127.         self.state
128.             .ensure_visible(matches_len, MAX_POPUP_ROWS.min(matches_len));
129.     }
130. 
131.     /// Determine the preferred height of the popup for a given width.
132.     /// Accounts for wrapped descriptions so that long tooltips don't overflow.
133.     pub(crate) fn calculate_required_height(&self, width: u16) -> u16 {
134.         let rows = self.rows_from_matches(self.filtered());
135. 
136.         measure_rows_height_with_col_width_mode(
137.             &rows,
138.             &self.state,
139.             MAX_POPUP_ROWS,
140.             width,
141.             COMMAND_COLUMN_WIDTH,
142.         )
143.     }
144. 
145.     /// Compute exact/prefix matches over built-in commands and user prompts,
146.     /// paired with optional highlight indices. Preserves the original
147.     /// presentation order for built-ins and prompts.
148.     fn filtered(&self) -> Vec<(CommandItem, Option<Vec<usize>>)> {
149.         let filter = self.command_filter.trim();
150.         let mut out: Vec<(CommandItem, Option<Vec<usize>>)> = Vec::new();
151.         if filter.is_empty() {
152.             for command in self.commands.iter() {
153.                 if matches!(command, CommandItem::Builtin(cmd) if ALIAS_COMMANDS.contains(cmd)) {
154.                     continue;
155.                 }
156.                 out.push((command.clone(), None));
157.             }
158.             return out;
159.         }
160. 
161.         let filter_lower = filter.to_lowercase();
162.         let filter_chars = filter.chars().count();
163.         let mut exact: Vec<(CommandItem, Option<Vec<usize>>)> = Vec::new();
164.         let mut prefix: Vec<(CommandItem, Option<Vec<usize>>)> = Vec::new();
165.         let indices_for = |offset| Some((offset..offset + filter_chars).collect());
166. 
167.         let mut push_match =
168.             |item: CommandItem, display: &str, name: Option<&str>, name_offset: usize| {
169.                 let display_lower = display.to_lowercase();
170.                 let name_lower = name.map(str::to_lowercase);
171.                 let display_exact = display_lower == filter_lower;
172.                 let name_exact = name_lower.as_deref() == Some(filter_lower.as_str());
173.                 if display_exact || name_exact {
174.                     let offset = if display_exact { 0 } else { name_offset };
175.                     exact.push((item, indices_for(offset)));
176.                     return;
177.                 }
178.                 let display_prefix = display_lower.starts_with(&filter_lower);
179.                 let name_prefix = name_lower
180.                     .as_ref()
181.                     .is_some_and(|name| name.starts_with(&filter_lower));
182.                 if display_prefix || name_prefix {
183.                     let offset = if display_prefix { 0 } else { name_offset };
184.                     prefix.push((item, indices_for(offset)));
185.                 }
186.             };
187. 
188.         for command in self.commands.iter() {
189.             let display = command.command();
190.             push_match(command.clone(), display, None, 0);
191.         }
192. 
193.         out.extend(exact);
194.         out.extend(prefix);
195.         out
196.     }
197. 
198.     fn filtered_items(&self) -> Vec<CommandItem> {
199.         self.filtered().into_iter().map(|(c, _)| c).collect()
200.     }
201. 
202.     fn rows_from_matches(
203.         &self,
204.         matches: Vec<(CommandItem, Option<Vec<usize>>)>,
205.     ) -> Vec<GenericDisplayRow> {
206.         matches
207.             .into_iter()
208.             .map(|(item, indices)| {
209.                 let name = format!("/{}", item.command());
210.                 let description = item.description().to_string();
211.                 GenericDisplayRow {
212.                     name,
213.                     name_prefix_spans: Vec::new(),
214.                     match_indices: indices.map(|v| v.into_iter().map(|i| i + 1).collect()),
215.                     display_shortcut: None,
216.                     description: Some(description),
217.                     category_tag: None,
218.                     wrap_indent: None,
219.                     is_disabled: false,
220.                     disabled_reason: None,
221.                 }
222.             })
223.             .collect()
224.     }
225. 
226.     /// Move the selection cursor one step up.
227.     pub(crate) fn move_up(&mut self) {
228.         let len = self.filtered_items().len();
229.         self.state.move_up_wrap(len);
230.         self.state.ensure_visible(len, MAX_POPUP_ROWS.min(len));
231.     }
232. 
233.     /// Move the selection cursor one step down.
234.     pub(crate) fn move_down(&mut self) {
235.         let matches_len = self.filtered_items().len();
236.         self.state.move_down_wrap(matches_len);
237.         self.state
238.             .ensure_visible(matches_len, MAX_POPUP_ROWS.min(matches_len));
239.     }
240. 
241.     /// Return currently selected command, if any.
242.     pub(crate) fn selected_item(&self) -> Option<CommandItem> {
243.         let matches = self.filtered_items();
244.         self.state
245.             .selected_idx
246.             .and_then(|idx| matches.get(idx).cloned())
247.     }
248. }
249. 
250. impl CommandItem {
251.     pub(crate) fn command(&self) -> &str {
252.         match self {
253.             Self::Builtin(cmd) => cmd.command(),
254.             Self::ServiceTier(command) => &command.name,
255.         }
256.     }
257. 
258.     fn description(&self) -> &str {
259.         match self {
260.             Self::Builtin(cmd) => cmd.description(),
```

</details>

1. //! TUI token usage models and display formatting.
2. 
3. use std::fmt;
4. 
5. use codex_protocol::num_format::format_with_separators;
6. use serde::Deserialize;
7. use serde::Serialize;
8. 
9. const BASELINE_TOKENS: i64 = 12000;
10. 
11. #[derive(Debug, Clone, Default, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize, Deserialize)]
12. pub struct TokenUsage {
13.     pub input_tokens: i64,
14.     pub cached_input_tokens: i64,
15.     pub output_tokens: i64,
16.     pub reasoning_output_tokens: i64,
17.     pub total_tokens: i64,
18. }
19. 
20. impl TokenUsage {
21.     pub fn is_zero(&self) -> bool {
22.         self.total_tokens == 0
23.     }
24. 
25.     pub(crate) fn cached_input(&self) -> i64 {
26.         self.cached_input_tokens.max(0)
27.     }
28. 
29.     pub(crate) fn non_cached_input(&self) -> i64 {
30.         (self.input_tokens - self.cached_input()).max(0)
31.     }
32. 
33.     pub(crate) fn blended_total(&self) -> i64 {
34.         (self.non_cached_input() + self.output_tokens.max(0)).max(0)
35.     }
36. 
37.     /// Returns the raw `total_tokens` value. For `last_token_usage`, this is the latest active
38.     /// context size; for `total_token_usage`, this is the accumulated session total.
39.     pub(crate) fn tokens_in_context_window(&self) -> i64 {
40.         self.total_tokens
41.     }
42. 
43.     pub(crate) fn percent_of_context_window_remaining(&self, context_window: i64) -> i64 {
44.         if context_window <= BASELINE_TOKENS {
45.             return 0;
46.         }
47.         let effective_window = context_window - BASELINE_TOKENS;
48.         let used = (self.tokens_in_context_window() - BASELINE_TOKENS).max(0);
49.         let remaining = (effective_window - used).max(0);
50.         ((remaining as f64 / effective_window as f64) * 100.0)
51.             .clamp(0.0, 100.0)
52.             .round() as i64
53.     }
54. }
55. 
56. #[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize, Deserialize)]
57. pub(crate) struct TokenUsageInfo {
58.     pub(crate) total_token_usage: TokenUsage,
59.     pub(crate) last_token_usage: TokenUsage,
60.     pub(crate) model_context_window: Option<i64>,
61. }
62. 
63. impl fmt::Display for TokenUsage {
64.     fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {
65.         write!(
66.             f,
67.             "Token usage: total={} input={}{} output={}{}",
68.             format_with_separators(self.blended_total()),
69.             format_with_separators(self.non_cached_input()),
70.             if self.cached_input() > 0 {
71.                 format!(
72.                     " (+ {} cached)",
73.                     format_with_separators(self.cached_input())
74.                 )
75.             } else {
76.                 String::new()
77.             },
78.             format_with_separators(self.output_tokens),
79.             if self.reasoning_output_tokens > 0 {
80.                 format!(
81.                     " (reasoning {})",
82.                     format_with_separators(self.reasoning_output_tokens)
83.                 )
84.             } else {
85.                 String::new()
86.             }
87.         )
88.     }
89. }
90.
```

51.     inline_message: Option<String>,

63. // Format elapsed seconds into a compact human-friendly form used by the status line.
64. // Examples: 0s, 59s, 1m 00s, 59m 59s, 1h 00m 00s, 2h 03m 09s
65. pub fn fmt_elapsed_compact(elapsed_secs: u64) -> String {
66.     if elapsed_secs < 60 {
67.         return format!("{elapsed_secs}s");
68.     }
69.     if elapsed_secs < 3600 {
70.         let minutes = elapsed_secs / 60;
71.         let seconds = elapsed_secs % 60;
72.         return format!("{minutes}m {seconds:02}s");
73.     }
74.     let hours = elapsed_secs / 3600;
75.     let minutes = (elapsed_secs % 3600) / 60;
76.     let seconds = elapsed_secs % 60;
77.     format!("{hours}h {minutes:02}m {seconds:02}s")
78. }
79.

214.             .subsequent_indent(Line::from(Span::from(" ".repeat(prefix_width)).dim()))
215.             .break_words(/*break_words*/ true);
216. 
217.         let mut out = word_wrap_lines(details.lines().map(|line| vec![line.dim()]), opts);
218. 
219.         if out.len() > self.details_max_lines {
220.             out.truncate(self.details_max_lines);

84. impl StatusHistoryHandle {
85.     pub(crate) fn finish_rate_limit_refresh(
86.         &self,
87.         rate_limits: &[RateLimitSnapshotDisplay],
88.         now: DateTime<Local>,
89.     ) {
90.         let rate_limits = if rate_limits.len() <= 1 {
91.             compose_rate_limit_data(rate_limits.first(), now)
92.         } else {
93.             compose_rate_limit_data_many(rate_limits, now)
94.         };
95.         #[expect(clippy::expect_used)]
96.         let mut state = self
97.             .rate_limit_state
98.             .write()
99.             .expect("status history rate-limit state poisoned");
100.         state.rate_limits = rate_limits;
101.         state.refreshing_rate_limits = false;
102.     }
103. }

376.     fn token_usage_spans(&self) -> Vec<Span<'static>> {
377.         let total_fmt = format_tokens_compact(self.token_usage.total);
378.         let input_fmt = format_tokens_compact(self.token_usage.input);

380.

394.     fn context_window_spans(&self) -> Option<Vec<Span<'static>>> {
395.         let context = self.token_usage.context_window.as_ref()?;
396.         let percent = context.percent_remaining;
397.         let used_fmt = format_tokens_compact(context.tokens_in_context);
398.         let window_fmt = format_tokens_compact(context.window);
399. 
400.         Some(vec![
401.             Span::from(format!("{percent}% left")),
402.             Span::from(" (").dim(),
403.             Span::from(used_fmt).dim(),
404.             Span::from(" used / ").dim(),
405.             Span::from(window_fmt).dim(),
406.             Span::from(")").dim(),
407.         ])
408.     }
409. 
410.     fn rate_limit_lines(
411.         &self,
412.         state: &StatusRateLimitState,
413.         available_inner_width: usize,
414.         formatter: &FieldFormatter,
415.     ) -> Vec<Line<'static>> {
416.         match &state.rate_limits {
417.             StatusRateLimitData::Available(rows_data) => {
418.                 if rows_data.is_empty() {
419.                     return vec![formatter.line(
420.                         "Limits",
421.                         vec![Span::from("not available for this account").dim()],
422.                     )];
423.                 }
424. 
425.                 self.rate_limit_row_lines(rows_data, available_inner_width, formatter)
426.             }
427.             StatusRateLimitData::Stale(rows_data) => {
428.                 let mut lines =
429.                     self.rate_limit_row_lines(rows_data, available_inner_width, formatter);
430.                 lines.push(formatter.line(
431.                     "Warning",
432.                     vec![Span::from(if state.refreshing_rate_limits {
433.                         "limits may be stale - run /status again shortly."
434.                     } else {
435.                         "limits may be stale - start new turn to refresh."
436.                     })
437.                     .dim()],
438.                 ));
439.                 lines
440.             }
441.             StatusRateLimitData::Unavailable => {
442.                 vec![formatter.line(
443.                     "Limits",
444.                     vec![Span::from("not available for this account").dim()],
445.                 )]
446.             }
447.             StatusRateLimitData::Missing => {
448.                 vec![formatter.line(
449.                     "Limits",
450.                     vec![Span::from(if state.refreshing_rate_limits {
451.                         "refresh requested; run /status again shortly."
452.                     } else {
453.                         "data not available yet"
454.                     })
455.                     .dim()],
456.                 )]
457.             }
458.         }
459.     }
460. 
461.     fn rate_limit_row_lines(
462.         &self,
463.         rows: &[StatusRateLimitRow],
464.         available_inner_width: usize,
465.         formatter: &FieldFormatter,
466.     ) -> Vec<Line<'static>> {
467.         let mut lines = Vec::with_capacity(rows.len().saturating_mul(2));
468. 
469.         for row in rows {
470.             match &row.value {
471.                 StatusRateLimitValue::Window {
472.                     percent_used,
473.                     resets_at,
474.                     details,
475.                 } => {
476.                     let percent_remaining = (100.0 - percent_used).clamp(0.0, 100.0);
477.                     let summary = format_status_limit_summary(percent_remaining);
478.                     let full_value_spans = vec![
479.                         Span::from(render_status_limit_progress_bar(percent_remaining)),
480.                         Span::from(" "),
481.                         Span::from(summary.clone()),
482.                     ];
483.                     // On narrow terminals, keep the percentage visible rather than
484.                     // letting the fixed-width progress bar crowd out the reset time.
485.                     let value_spans = if line_display_width(&Line::from(full_value_spans.clone()))
486.                         <= formatter.value_width(available_inner_width)
487.                     {
488.                         full_value_spans
489.                     } else {
490.                         vec![Span::from(summary)]
491.                     };
492.                     let base_spans = formatter.full_spans(row.label.as_str(), value_spans);
493.                     let base_line = Line::from(base_spans.clone());
494. 
495.                     if let Some(resets_at) = resets_at.as_ref() {
496.                         let resets_span = Span::from(format!("(resets {resets_at})")).dim();
497.                         let mut inline_spans = base_spans.clone();
498.                         inline_spans.push(Span::from(" ").dim());
499.                         inline_spans.push(resets_span.clone());
500. 
501.                         if line_display_width(&Line::from(inline_spans.clone()))
502.                             <= available_inner_width
503.                         {
504.                             lines.push(Line::from(inline_spans));
505.                         } else {
506.                             lines.push(base_line);
507.                             let reset_text = format!("(resets {resets_at})");
508.                             let reset_width = formatter.value_width(available_inner_width).max(1);
509.                             let wrap_options =
510.                                 textwrap::Options::new(reset_width).break_words(false);
511.                             // Reset timestamps are the actionable part of this row, so wrap them
512.                             // onto continuation lines instead of truncating partial times/dates.
513.                             lines.extend(
514.                                 textwrap::wrap(reset_text.as_str(), wrap_options)
515.                                     .into_iter()
516.                                     .map(|wrapped| {
517.                                         formatter.continuation(vec![
518.                                             Span::from(wrapped.into_owned()).dim(),
519.                                         ])
520.                                     }),
```

20. #[derive(Clone, Debug, PartialEq)]

27. pub(super) struct AttachmentState {

30.     pub(super) selected_remote_image_index: Option<usize>,
31. }
32. 
33. impl AttachmentState {
34.     pub(super) fn is_empty(&self) -> bool {
35.         self.local_images.is_empty() && self.remote_image_urls.is_empty()
36.     }
37. 
38.     pub(super) fn local_image_paths(&self) -> Vec<PathBuf> {
39.         self.local_images
40.             .iter()
41.             .map(|image| image.path.clone())
42.             .collect()
43.     }

46.         self.local_images
47.             .iter()
48.             .map(|image| LocalImageAttachment {
49.                 placeholder: image.placeholder.clone(),
50.                 path: image.path.clone(),
51.             })
52.             .collect()
53.     }
54. 
55.     pub(super) fn set_remote_image_urls(&mut self, urls: Vec<String>, textarea: &mut TextArea) {
56.         self.remote_image_urls = urls;
57.         self.selected_remote_image_index = None;
58.         self.relabel_local_images(textarea);
59.     }
60.

62.         self.remote_image_urls.clone()
63.     }
64. 
65.     pub(super) fn take_remote_image_urls(&mut self, textarea: &mut TextArea) -> Vec<String> {
66.         let urls = std::mem::take(&mut self.remote_image_urls);
67.         self.selected_remote_image_index = None;
68.         self.relabel_local_images(textarea);
69.         urls
70.     }
71. 
72.     pub(super) fn clear_remote_image_urls(&mut self) {
73.         self.remote_image_urls.clear();
74.         self.selected_remote_image_index = None;
75.     }
76. 
77.     pub(super) fn reset_local_images(
78.         &mut self,
79.         local_image_paths: Vec<PathBuf>,
80.         textarea: &mut TextArea,
81.     ) {
82.         self.local_images.clear();
83.         self.local_images.extend(

89.                     path,
90.                 }),
91.         );
92.         self.selected_remote_image_index = None;
93.         self.relabel_local_images(textarea);
94.     }
95. 
96.     pub(super) fn attach_image(&mut self, textarea: &mut TextArea, path: PathBuf) {
97.         let image_number = self.remote_image_urls.len() + self.local_images.len() + 1;
98.         let placeholder = local_image_label_text(image_number);
99.         textarea.insert_element(&placeholder);
100.         self.local_images.push(AttachedImage { placeholder, path });
101.     }
102. 
103.     pub(super) fn prune_local_images_for_submission(
104.         &mut self,
105.         text: &str,
106.         text_elements: &[TextElement],
107.     ) {
108.         if self.local_images.is_empty() {
109.             return;
110.         }
111. 
112.         let image_placeholders: HashSet<&str> = text_elements
113.             .iter()
114.             .filter_map(|element| element.placeholder(text))
115.             .collect();
116.         self.local_images
117.             .retain(|image| image_placeholders.contains(image.placeholder.as_str()));
118.     }
119. 
120.     #[cfg(test)]

139. 
140.     pub(super) fn remote_image_lines(&self) -> Vec<Line<'static>> {
141.         self.remote_image_urls
142.             .iter()
143.             .enumerate()
144.             .map(|(index, _)| {
145.                 let label = local_image_label_text(index + 1);
146.                 if self.selected_remote_image_index == Some(index) {
147.                     label.cyan().reversed().into()
148.                 } else {
149.                     label.cyan().into()
150.                 }
151.             })
152.             .collect()
153.     }
154. 
155.     pub(super) fn clear_remote_image_selection(&mut self) {
156.         self.selected_remote_image_index = None;
157.     }
158. 
159.     pub(super) fn handle_remote_image_selection_key(
160.         &mut self,
161.         key_event: &KeyEvent,
162.         textarea: &mut TextArea,
163.     ) -> Option<(InputResult, bool)> {
164.         if self.remote_image_urls.is_empty()
165.             || key_event.modifiers != KeyModifiers::NONE
166.             || key_event.kind != KeyEventKind::Press
167.         {
168.             return None;
169.         }
170. 
171.         match key_event.code {
172.             KeyCode::Up => {
173.                 if let Some(selected) = self.selected_remote_image_index {
174.                     self.selected_remote_image_index = Some(selected.saturating_sub(1));
175.                     Some((InputResult::None, true))
176.                 } else if textarea.cursor() == 0 {
177.                     self.selected_remote_image_index = Some(self.remote_image_urls.len() - 1);
178.                     Some((InputResult::None, true))
179.                 } else {
180.                     None
181.                 }
182.             }
183.             KeyCode::Down => {
184.                 if let Some(selected) = self.selected_remote_image_index {
185.                     if selected + 1 < self.remote_image_urls.len() {
186.                         self.selected_remote_image_index = Some(selected + 1);
187.                     } else {
188.                         self.clear_remote_image_selection();
189.                     }
190.                     Some((InputResult::None, true))
191.                 } else {
192.                     None
193.                 }
194.             }
195.             KeyCode::Delete | KeyCode::Backspace => {
196.                 if let Some(selected) = self.selected_remote_image_index {
197.                     self.remove_selected_remote_image(selected, textarea);
198.                     Some((InputResult::None, true))
199.                 } else {
200.                     None
201.                 }
202.             }
203.             _ => None,
204.         }
205.     }
206. 
207.     pub(super) fn remove_deleted_local_placeholders(
208.         &mut self,
209.         removed_payloads: &[String],

211.     ) -> bool {

214.             !removed_payloads
215.                 .iter()
216.                 .any(|payload| payload == &image.placeholder)
217.         });
218.         let removed_any = self.local_images.len() != previous_len;
219.         if removed_any {
220.             self.relabel_local_images(textarea);

### ✅ `view`

**view the file at /Users/nick/CascadeProjects/codex/codex-rs/tui/src/bottom_pane/paste_burst.rs.**

/Users/nick/CascadeProjects/codex/codex-rs/tui/src/bottom_pane/paste_burst.rs (lines 1-220)

<details>
<summary>220 lines</summary>

```
1. //! Paste-burst detection for terminals without bracketed paste.
2. //!
3. //! On some platforms (notably Windows), pastes often arrive as a rapid stream of
4. //! `KeyCode::Char` and `KeyCode::Enter` key events rather than as a single "paste" event.
5. //! In that mode, the composer needs to:
6. //!
7. //! - Prevent transient UI side effects (e.g. toggles bound to `?`) from triggering on pasted text.
8. //! - Ensure Enter is treated as a newline *inside the paste*, not as "submit the message".
9. //! - Avoid flicker caused by inserting a typed prefix and then immediately reclassifying it as
10. //!   paste once enough chars have arrived.
11. //!
12. //! This module provides the `PasteBurst` state machine. `ChatComposer` feeds it only "plain"
13. //! character events (no Ctrl/Alt) and uses the full buffering decisions to either:
14. //!
15. //! - briefly hold a first ASCII char (flicker suppression),
16. //! - buffer a burst as a single pasted string, or
17. //! - let input flow through as normal typing.
18. //!
19. //! # Call Pattern
20. //!
21. //! `PasteBurst` is a pure state machine: it never mutates the textarea directly. The caller feeds
22. //! it events and then applies the chosen action:
23. //!
24. //! - For each plain `KeyCode::Char`, call [`PasteBurst::on_plain_char`] (ASCII) or
25. //!   [`PasteBurst::on_plain_char_no_hold`] (non-ASCII/IME).
26. //! - If the decision indicates buffering, the caller appends to `PasteBurst.buffer` via
27. //!   [`PasteBurst::append_char_to_buffer`].
28. //! - On a UI tick, call [`PasteBurst::flush_if_due`]. If it returns [`FlushResult::Typed`], insert
29. //!   that char as normal typing. If it returns [`FlushResult::Paste`], treat the returned string as
30. //!   an explicit paste.
31. //! - Before applying non-char input (arrow keys, Ctrl/Alt modifiers, etc.), use
32. //!   [`PasteBurst::flush_before_modified_input`] to avoid leaving buffered text "stuck", and then
33. //!   [`PasteBurst::clear_window_after_non_char`] so subsequent typing does not get grouped into a
34. //!   previous burst.
35. //! - Direct-insert callers can skip buffering, use
36. //!   [`PasteBurst::direct_insert_newline_should_insert`] in their Enter handler, and call
37. //!   [`PasteBurst::extend_window`] when Enter or [`PasteBurst::on_plain_char_no_hold`] reports a
38. //!   burst-like stream.
39. //!
40. //! # State Variables
41. //!
42. //! This state machine is encoded in a few fields with slightly different meanings:
43. //!
44. //! - `active`: true while we are still *actively* accepting characters into the current burst.
45. //! - `buffer`: accumulated burst text that will eventually flush as a single `Paste(String)`.
46. //!   A non-empty buffer is treated as "in burst context" even if `active` has been cleared.
47. //! - `pending_first_char`: a single held ASCII char used for flicker suppression. The caller must
48. //!   not render this char until it either becomes part of a burst (`BeginBufferFromPending`) or
49. //!   flushes as a normal typed char (`FlushResult::Typed`).
50. //! - `last_plain_char_time`/`consecutive_plain_char_burst`: the timing/count heuristic for
51. //!   "paste-like" streams.
52. //! - `burst_window_until`: the Enter suppression window ("Enter inserts newline") that outlives the
53. //!   buffer itself.
54. //!
55. //! # Timing Model
56. //!
57. //! There are two timeouts:
58. //!
59. //! - `PASTE_BURST_CHAR_INTERVAL`: maximum delay between consecutive "plain" chars for them to be
60. //!   considered part of a single burst. It also bounds how long `pending_first_char` is held.
61. //! - `PASTE_BURST_ACTIVE_IDLE_TIMEOUT`: once buffering is active, how long to wait after the last
62. //!   char before flushing the accumulated buffer as a paste.
63. //!
64. //! `flush_if_due()` intentionally uses `>` (not `>=`) when comparing elapsed time, so tests and UI
65. //! ticks should cross the threshold by at least 1ms (see `recommended_flush_delay()`).
66. //!
67. //! # Retro Capture Details
68. //!
69. //! Retro-capture exists to handle the case where we initially inserted characters as "normal
70. //! typing", but later decide that the stream is paste-like. When that happens, we retroactively
71. //! remove a prefix of already-inserted text from the textarea and move it into the burst buffer so
72. //! the eventual `handle_paste(...)` sees a contiguous pasted string.
73. //!
74. //! Retro-capture mostly matters on paths that do *not* hold the first character (non-ASCII/IME
75. //! input, and retro-grab scenarios). The ASCII path usually prefers
76. //! `RetainFirstChar -> BeginBufferFromPending`, which avoids needing retro-capture at all.
77. //!
78. //! Retro-capture is expressed in terms of characters, not bytes:
79. //!
80. //! - `CharDecision::BeginBuffer { retro_chars }` uses `retro_chars` as a character count.
81. //! - `decide_begin_buffer(now, before_cursor, retro_chars)` turns that into a UTF-8 byte range by
82. //!   calling `retro_start_index()`.
83. //! - `RetroGrab.start_byte` is a byte index into the `before_cursor` slice; callers must clamp the
84. //!   cursor to a char boundary before slicing so `start_byte..cursor` is always valid UTF-8.
85. //!
86. //! # Clearing vs Flushing
87. //!
88. //! There are two ways callers end burst handling, and they are not interchangeable:
89. //!
90. //! - `flush_before_modified_input()` returns the buffered text (and/or a pending first ASCII char)
91. //!   so the caller can apply it through the normal paste path before handling an unrelated input.
92. //! - `clear_window_after_non_char()` clears the *classification window* so subsequent typing does
93. //!   not get grouped into the previous burst. It assumes the caller has already flushed any buffer
94. //!   because it clears `last_plain_char_time`, which means `flush_if_due()` will not flush a
95. //!   non-empty buffer until another plain char updates the timestamp.
96. //!
97. //! # States (Conceptually)
98. //!
99. //! - **Idle**: no buffered text, no pending char.
100. //! - **Pending first char**: `pending_first_char` holds one ASCII char for up to
101. //!   `PASTE_BURST_CHAR_INTERVAL` while we wait to see if a burst follows.
102. //! - **Active buffer**: `active`/`buffer` holds paste-like content until it times out and flushes.
103. //! - **Enter suppress window**: `burst_window_until` keeps Enter treated as newline briefly after
104. //!   burst activity so multiline pastes stay grouped.
105. //!
106. //! # ASCII vs Non-ASCII
107. //!
108. //! - [`PasteBurst::on_plain_char`] may return [`CharDecision::RetainFirstChar`] to hold the first
109. //!   ASCII char and avoid flicker.
110. //! - [`PasteBurst::on_plain_char_no_hold`] never holds (used for IME/non-ASCII paths), since
111. //!   holding a non-ASCII character can feel like dropped input.
112. //!
113. //! # Contract With Callers
114. //!
115. //! `PasteBurst` does not mutate the UI text buffer on its own. Callers must interpret decisions
116. //! and apply the corresponding UI edits. `ChatComposer` uses the full buffering contract:
117. //!
118. //! - For each plain ASCII `KeyCode::Char`, call [`PasteBurst::on_plain_char`].
119. //!   - [`CharDecision::RetainFirstChar`]: do **not** insert the char into the textarea yet.
120. //!   - [`CharDecision::BeginBufferFromPending`]: call [`PasteBurst::append_char_to_buffer`] for the
121. //!     current char (the previously-held char is already in the burst buffer).
122. //!   - [`CharDecision::BeginBuffer { retro_chars }`]: consider retro-capturing the already-inserted
123. //!     prefix by calling [`PasteBurst::decide_begin_buffer`]. If it returns `Some`, remove the
124. //!     returned `start_byte..cursor` range from the textarea and then call
125. //!     [`PasteBurst::append_char_to_buffer`] for the current char. If it returns `None`, fall back
126. //!     to normal insertion.
127. //!   - [`CharDecision::BufferAppend`]: call [`PasteBurst::append_char_to_buffer`].
128. //!
129. //! - For each plain non-ASCII `KeyCode::Char`, call [`PasteBurst::on_plain_char_no_hold`] and then:
130. //!   - If it returns `Some(CharDecision::BufferAppend)`, call
131. //!     [`PasteBurst::append_char_to_buffer`].
132. //!   - If it returns `Some(CharDecision::BeginBuffer { retro_chars })`, call
133. //!     [`PasteBurst::decide_begin_buffer`] as above (and if buffering starts, remove the grabbed
134. //!     prefix from the textarea and then append the current char to the buffer).
135. //!   - If it returns `None`, insert normally.
136. //!
137. //! - Before applying non-char input (or any input that should not join a burst), call
138. //!   [`PasteBurst::flush_before_modified_input`] and pass the returned string (if any) through the
139. //!   normal paste path.
140. //!
141. //! - Periodically (e.g. on a UI tick), call [`PasteBurst::flush_if_due`].
142. //!   - [`FlushResult::Typed`]: insert that single char as normal typing.
143. //!   - [`FlushResult::Paste`]: treat the returned string as an explicit paste.
144. //!
145. //! - When a non-plain key is pressed (Ctrl/Alt-modified input, arrows, etc.), callers should use
146. //!   [`PasteBurst::clear_window_after_non_char`] to prevent the next keystroke from being
147. //!   incorrectly grouped into a previous burst.
148. 
149. use std::time::Duration;
150. use std::time::Instant;
151. 
152. // Heuristic thresholds for detecting paste-like input bursts.
153. // Detect quickly to avoid showing typed prefix before paste is recognized
154. const PASTE_BURST_MIN_CHARS: u16 = 3;
155. const PASTE_ENTER_SUPPRESS_WINDOW: Duration = Duration::from_millis(120);
156. 
157. // Maximum delay between consecutive chars to be considered part of a paste burst.
158. const PASTE_BURST_CHAR_INTERVAL: Duration = Duration::from_millis(8);
159. 
160. // Idle timeout before flushing buffered paste content.
161. // Slower paste bursts have been observed in Windows environments.
162. #[cfg(not(windows))]
163. const PASTE_BURST_ACTIVE_IDLE_TIMEOUT: Duration = Duration::from_millis(8);
164. #[cfg(windows)]
165. const PASTE_BURST_ACTIVE_IDLE_TIMEOUT: Duration = Duration::from_millis(60);
166. 
167. #[derive(Default)]
168. pub(crate) struct PasteBurst {
169.     last_plain_char_time: Option<Instant>,
170.     consecutive_plain_char_burst: u16,
171.     burst_window_until: Option<Instant>,
172.     buffer: String,
173.     active: bool,
174.     // Hold first fast char briefly to avoid rendering flicker
175.     pending_first_char: Option<(char, Instant)>,
176. }
177. 
178. pub(crate) enum CharDecision {
179.     /// Start buffering and retroactively capture some already-inserted chars.
180.     BeginBuffer { retro_chars: u16 },
181.     /// We are currently buffering; append the current char into the buffer.
182.     BufferAppend,
183.     /// Do not insert/render this char yet; temporarily save the first fast
184.     /// char while we wait to see if a paste-like burst follows.
185.     RetainFirstChar,
186.     /// Begin buffering using the previously saved first char (no retro grab needed).
187.     BeginBufferFromPending,
188. }
189. 
190. pub(crate) struct RetroGrab {
191.     pub start_byte: usize,
192.     pub grabbed: String,
193. }
194. 
195. pub(crate) enum FlushResult {
196.     Paste(String),
197.     Typed(char),
198.     None,
199. }
200. 
201. impl PasteBurst {
202.     /// Recommended delay to wait between simulated keypresses (or before
203.     /// scheduling a UI tick) so that a pending fast keystroke is flushed
204.     /// out of the burst detector as normal typed input.
205.     ///
206.     /// Primarily used by tests and by the TUI to reliably cross the
207.     /// paste-burst timing threshold.
208.     pub fn recommended_flush_delay() -> Duration {
209.         PASTE_BURST_CHAR_INTERVAL + Duration::from_millis(1)
210.     }
211. 
212.     #[cfg(test)]
213.     pub(crate) fn recommended_active_flush_delay() -> Duration {
214.         PASTE_BURST_ACTIVE_IDLE_TIMEOUT + Duration::from_millis(1)
215.     }
216. 
217.     /// Entry point: decide how to treat a plain char with current timing.
218.     pub fn on_plain_char(&mut self, ch: char, now: Instant) -> CharDecision {
219.         self.note_plain_char(now);
220.
```
